  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0ab97ba6-95ab-4cab-b2ba-dfa6e07d17ad'
      });

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer5208274946104775322">October "Toby" Daye is a changeling, the daughter of Amandine of the fae and a mortal man. Like her mother, she is gifted in blood magic, able to read what has happened to a person through a mere taste of blood. Toby is the only changeling who has earned knighthood, and she re-earns that position every day, undertaking assignments for her liege, Sylvester, the Duke of the </span>
  <span id="freeText5208274946104775322" style="display:none">October "Toby" Daye is a changeling, the daughter of Amandine of the fae and a mortal man. Like her mother, she is gifted in blood magic, able to read what has happened to a person through a mere taste of blood. Toby is the only changeling who has earned knighthood, and she re-earns that position every day, undertaking assignments for her liege, Sylvester, the Duke of the Shadowed Hills.<br /><br />Now Sylvester has asked her to go to the County of Tamed Lightning—otherwise known as Fremont, CA—to make sure that all is well with his niece, Countess January O'Leary, whom he has not been able to contact. It seems like a simple enough assignment—but when dealing with the realm of Faerie nothing is ever as simple as it seems. Toby soon discovers that someone has begun murdering people close to January, whose domain is a buffer between Sylvester's realm and a scheming rival duchy. If Toby can't find the killer soon, she may well become the next victim.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5208274946104775322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351714551" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/351714551?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/7884731-a-local-habitation">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer351714551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer202915046418934962"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2016/03/review-a-local-habitation-by-seanan-mcguire-jessicadhaluska-seananmcguire-dawbooks.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>When we left October at the end of ROSEMARY AND RUE, she had resumed her life as a changeling, existing to varying degrees in both the human and fae worlds. She'd gotten her PI license renewed, and things were altogether looking up for her, b/c she'd finally stopped ostriching. <br/><br/>A LOCAL HABITATION begins with a somewhat drunken October and a couple of her changeling friends wrapping up a girls night out. <br/><br/>It's an October we haven't seen before, I bloody love it:<br/><br/><blockquote>
<i>“T</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText202915046418934962" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2016/03/review-a-local-habitation-by-seanan-mcguire-jessicadhaluska-seananmcguire-dawbooks.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br>When we left October at the end of ROSEMARY AND RUE, she had resumed her life as a changeling, existing to varying degrees in both the human and fae worlds. She'd gotten her PI license renewed, and things were altogether looking up for her, b/c she'd finally stopped ostriching. <br><br>A LOCAL HABITATION begins with a somewhat drunken October and a couple of her changeling friends wrapping up a girls night out. <br><br>It's an October we haven't seen before, I bloody love it:<br><br><blockquote>
<i>“The skirt passes muster,” said Tybalt, finishing his survey. “I might have called it a ‘belt’ rather than a ‘skirt,’ but I suppose you have the right to name your own clothing. While we’re on the subject of apparel, tell me, were you intending to walk all the way home in those shoes?” <br>“Maybe,” I hedged. The straps were starting to chafe my ankles, making walking even less comfortable than it had been to begin with, but </i>he<i> didn’t need to know that. <br><b>“You’re drunk, October.” <br>“And you’re wearing really tight pants.”</b></i>
</blockquote><br>*giggle snorts* *waves at Tybalt*<br><br>But, of course, things can't stay pleasantly intoxicated forever, or even for more than the occasional evening, and the following morning she wakes to both a hangover and a summons from her liege.<br><br>His niece is the countess of a politically significant county in between his land and the neighboring duchy, you see, and she's been out of contact. He's worried, but he can't check in on her himself without potentially creating a diplomatic incident.<br><br>Guess who can. <br><br>Oh, and here, take this manboy page with you, and teach him something, while you're at it.<br><br><b>There are two reasons this is my least favorite installment in the series:</b><br><br><b>1. Tech is the antithesis to all things Fae.</b><br><br>Two things are said to harm Fae:<br><br>Organized religion, b/c of the typical close-mindedness that is in direct opposition to the pagan beliefs from which the Fae sprung, and iron, b/c metaphor for urban expansion destroying/polluting the natural environment of Fae.<br><br>So Fae developing tech for their own personal use . . . and a dryad, a TREE fae, thriving in an artificial environment??<br><br>O_____O<br><br><b>2. The employees of ADH getting picked-off one by one like the cast of a horror movie.</b><br><br>I hate horror movies. <br><br>For a lot of reasons, but mostly b/c I'm chicken. The next biggest reason is b/c lack of character development. <br><br>Not that I blame an author--I mean, really? Why waste time on red shirts?--but all the same, that characteristic lack of development makes it feel like a lot of senseless death. <br><br>PLUS, even if there are a few of the newly introduced secondaries whom I would ordinarily like, I deliberately keep them at a distance, b/c there's an excellent chance their days are numbered, and I don't need the emotional trauma.<br><br>This is a problem b/c character-driven reader. <br><br>BUT. <br><br>Both of those things are obviously personal preference issues. Lots of people love it when an author takes universally accepted ideas and turns them on their heads, and there is more than enough plot and accompanying twists to keep most readers happy.<br><br>And overall, <i>I</i> was also happy. In any series, one of the books <i>must</i> have the dubious honor of being the least favorite. A LOCAL HABITATION just happens to be mine. BUT. Onwards and upwards, my friends, b/c the next book--what is it about third installments frequently being the game changer in a long-running series?--is fantastic. SO. Highly recommended, if only b/c you can't get to #3 without it. <br><br>ALSO, there's a handy pronunciation guide in the front of the book, and the names of specific types of Fae are just fun to say . . . <i>Lou-sha-k, Lou-sha-k, Lou-sha-k </i> . . . <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The October Day BR with <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">BB&amp;B</a>
</b> continues! BUT. I will say in advance that this is my least favorite installment. Fae and tech FREAKS me out. Just sayin'.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446128036i/16751969.jpg" width="255" height="361" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351653785" rel="nofollow noopener">Rosemary and Rue (October Daye, #1)</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351714504" rel="nofollow noopener">An Artificial Night (October Daye, #3)</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351592686" rel="nofollow noopener">Late Eclipses (October Daye, #4)</a>

<div id="review_1633107056" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1633107056" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1633107056?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1633107056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7128867527740499007">If it weren't for trusted friends telling me this gets better, I think I'd dump this series.<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463419926ra/19116696.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Why?<br/>Well, for starters, dumbassery <b>abounds</b> in book 2. If there's a cliche about <i>what not to do</i> when a serial killer is on the loose, then these idiots can't WAIT to do it!<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463419926ra/19116697.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Toby is called on by Sylvester to investigate why his niece isn't returning his phone calls. He can't go himself, because of Fairy politics (that I <i>still</i> don't entirely understand), which means she's basically on her own. Well, he send</span>
  <span id="freeText7128867527740499007" style="display:none">If it weren't for trusted friends telling me this gets better, I think I'd dump this series.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463419926ra/19116696.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Why?<br>Well, for starters, dumbassery <b>abounds</b> in book 2. If there's a cliche about <i>what not to do</i> when a serial killer is on the loose, then these idiots can't WAIT to do it!<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463419926ra/19116697.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Toby is called on by Sylvester to investigate why his niece isn't returning his phone calls. He can't go himself, because of Fairy politics (that I <i>still</i> don't entirely understand), which means she's basically on her own. Well, he sends Quentin along to help, but still...<br>Anyway.<br>From the moment she arrives at January's (&lt;--the niece) business/home/kingdom/whatever, nobody else had to die. Everything...and I mean <i>everything</i>...that happens from that point forward is sheer stupidity.<br><i>Butbutbutbut....</i><br>NO. And here's why:<br>Sylvester thought January was ignoring <i>his</i> phone calls, and when Toby gets there, she finds out that January thought her uncle was ignoring <i>her</i> phone calls. Now, what does that immediately tell you? <br><b>Someone on the inside has hijacked your phone lines! </b><br>Right? But for some reason they continue to try to use them to call out on, because that's such a <i>fantastic</i> idea.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463421693ra/19116921.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There were also a bunch of lame reasons why nobody would leave (including Toby &amp; Quentin) and just go get help. I would go into it, but I'd rather not rant and/or give any spoilers.<br>Needless to say, none of the excuses they used made enough sense (to me) to make the story relatable or realistic in any way. I just wanted to slap everyone. Everyone!<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463421985ra/19116943.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok. So while the mystery/horror stuff didn't quite do it for me, the thing that really worked my nerves was all the crying.<br><b>EMOTIONS! Emotions everywhere!</b><br>It felt like every time I flipped a page, someone was sobbing. <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463422467ra/19116996.gif" width="360" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463422467ra/19116997.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463425308ra/19117349.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463425308ra/19117350.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452630275ra/17720005.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah. Like that.<br>The main thing I learned about the fae in this book is that they're emotional wrecks, and incapable of removing themselves from imminent danger. <i>Great.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463428165ra/19117593.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Oh, and I figured out what the deal was with Alex &amp; Terri almost immediately. I mean, <i>come on!</i> It was incredibly obvious! Ugh!<br>The fact that the author dragged that <i>"mystery"</i> out till the very end kind of ticked me off. Mainly because I kept thinking that it had to be a cooler mystery than I thought. <br>But no.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463428718ra/19117627.gif" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>However</b>.<br>Many of my friends' reviews note that <i>this</i> is their least favorite book in the series, and several of them had the same problems with it that I had. And yet...they swear that this gets better.<br>Plus, I don't <i>hate</i> any of the characters, I'm just not <i>attached</i> to any of them right now. And the book wasn't unreadable, it just had annoying stuff happening.<br>So. Bottom line? I'm going to give <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6782468.An_Artificial_Night__October_Daye___3_" title="An Artificial Night (October Daye, #3) by Seanan McGuire" rel="nofollow noopener">An Artificial Night</a> a whirl. <br><i>What? </i> I believe my pals!<br>Besides, what's the worst that can happen?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463428165ra/19117595.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="7128867527740499007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1579946338" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1579946338" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1579946338?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=uf-pnr">uf-pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=beware-the-bermuda-love-triangle">beware-the-bermuda-love-triangle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1579946338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7586878829237861341"><b>3.5 You Are Growing on Me Stars</b><br/><br/>Buddy Read with the UF cravers at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books and Baubles</a><br/><br/>I didn’t initially fall head over heels in love with this series. And I’m still not totally in love….<b>but I feel like the first book was our first date and while it wasn’t the best first date I’ve ever been on it also wasn’t the worst.</b> On our first date Toby was dark and moody and most everything in the book seemed to take on a shade of that.<br/><br/>But Toby also didn’t break any of my huge no, no rules on our first</span>
  <span id="freeText7586878829237861341" style="display:none"><b>3.5 You Are Growing on Me Stars</b><br /><br />Buddy Read with the UF cravers at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a><br /><br />I didn’t initially fall head over heels in love with this series. And I’m still not totally in love….<b>but I feel like the first book was our first date and while it wasn’t the best first date I’ve ever been on it also wasn’t the worst.</b> On our first date Toby was dark and moody and most everything in the book seemed to take on a shade of that.<br /><br />But Toby also didn’t break any of my huge no, no rules on our first date and my book bff <a>Jessica</a> assured me this is a good series and I just need to give it a little time to grow on me. So with that I walked into the second book and it went better.<br /><br />This world is still a little more dark than some of the other UF I’ve read. But, the good news is that <b>some of the humor that I found lacking in the first book to counterbalance that darkness finally showed through a little.</b> Toby lightened up a little and with the help of a junior sidekick in training and King of the Cats there was a bit more humor throughout the story. Stuff like: <br /><blockquote><i>“Repetition is sometimes the best way to deal with the Luideag: just keep saying the same thing over and over until she gets fed up and gives you what you want. <b>All preschoolers have an instinctive grasp of this concept, but most don’t practice it on immortal water demons.</b> That’s probably why there are so few disembowelments in your average preschool.”</i><br /> <br /> AND<br /><br /><i>“Hey!" I turned, crossing my arms and glaring. "I was talking to him!"<br />Tybalt eyed me with amusement, which just made me glare harder. "No, you were inciting him to stab you with a toothpick. Again, the difference is small, but I think it matters.” </i></blockquote><br />Because I’d already been introduced to this world I got to sit back and just enjoy the story a little more. Since we are dealing with the Fae I try to remember that the rules for the immortals are different than humans. Actually for the most part as a Fae you are allowed to do anything you want to a human as long as you don’t get caught. Most of those things seem to be rather cruel and morally bankrupt but you have to remember that to them it is like playing with flies or ants so how bad should they feel about it.<br /><br />This overall story was way more interesting to me for a number of reasons. First the majority of the setting of this story is a Faery Tech Company. Fae and Computers….now this isn’t something I was expecting and so I found it a nice change up to the lore and a great way to bring it into the 2000s. It worked for me and (Second)<b> I totally loved the addition of a computer tree dryad. </b> YES!!! You read that right and I totally want one at my job too. Also the scene with the Night Haunts was creeptastic and probably one of the most interesting things in this series so far.<br /><br />While I did guess a few of the major twists….one super early it really didn’t take away from the overall enjoyment of most of the rest of the story as I tried to decide how it all fit in. I didn’t get to the complete who the killer was until much later in the story and then I totally got the reasons wrong but once explained it made total sense.<br /><br />While Toby is growing on me like Jessica told me she would the actual big seller for me is the world. It is a little different than most of the UF I’ve been reading since this is mostly Fae and the majority of other UF sticks with the shapeshifters, vampires and witches OH MY. So this has been a good switch up for me. Little snippets for the overall story arc seem to be included in this one and I now I have some serious questions about Toby’s mother and Tybalt who pretty much steals the show when he is on page.<br /><br />I would like it is there was maybe a more clear love interest at this time but that is where this story is lacking for me a little. <b>I’m standing on the SS Tybalt for sure but it seems like we are going to maybe have to travel through Hurricane Conner to get there</b> and I’m actually dreading the idea of that for a few reasons one being that he is totally married (<i>yes I know it is only a political marriage…..but I don’t care. I do not want Toby getting caught up in that mess, married is married</i>). <br /><br />So while I’m not in totally in love yet, our second date went much better and if this trend continues then this could easily make it into the space in my heart saved for Series I Love.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7586878829237861341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_69520695" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/69520695" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572638169p2/2016128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/69520695?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=color-yellow">color-yellow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=fairies">fairies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=dumb-female-characters">dumb-female-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=bought-2010">bought-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69520695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5750317582480212689">I really wanted to like this one. I did. <b>But it was bloated and Toby was a terrible detective.</b> Let me explain...<br/><br/><i>Toby gets a visit from Sylvester, her liege, just as she's starting to pick up the pieces of her life from the last book. He wants her to check on his niece, January, over in another kingdom because she hasn't check in for a few weeks. January's county is situated in between his and another Duchess's lands so if he goes to help her there would be political conflict. So he asks Toby to </i></span>
  <span id="freeText5750317582480212689" style="display:none">I really wanted to like this one. I did. <b>But it was bloated and Toby was a terrible detective.</b> Let me explain...<br /><br /><i>Toby gets a visit from Sylvester, her liege, just as she's starting to pick up the pieces of her life from the last book. He wants her to check on his niece, January, over in another kingdom because she hasn't check in for a few weeks. January's county is situated in between his and another Duchess's lands so if he goes to help her there would be political conflict. So he asks Toby to go instead and she agrees because she always helps him when he asks a favor. January is actually the boss at ALH, a computer company of sorts, and when Toby gets to the office building she finds out that all is definitely not alright with Sylvester's niece. And what Toby ends up uncovering is something she never could have dreamed up, and probably something she wishes she had never stumbled upon.</i><br /><br /><b>I'm gonna start with the positives.</b> I like the cover art for the book. I like that the author weaves in a lot of faerie lore that hasn't been overused in other novels. Tybalt is intriguing, but at this point, barely a bit player. Finding out what/who the nighthaunts are was also pretty cool. I appreciated the pronunciation guide at the beginning.<br /><br />Now, for the not so positives.<br /><br /><b>Toby is stupid.</b> Or at least, she shouldn't be a detective. Look for another line of work, girl. There were three main mysteries throughout the novel: Who was killing people, why they were doing it, and what exactly was going on with Alex and Terrie. <b>I figured out two of the three mysteries before the first 100 pages were up.</b> And with a book that was almost 400 pages, this was <i>incredibly</i> frustrating. I understand that as a reader we have better insight into the whole picture, but <i>come on.</i> I actually think most of the time I'm pretty dense when it comes to mysteries, but I felt like I was hit over the head <i>repeatedly</i> with who the villain was. I honestly don't understand why it took her so long to put the pieces together.<br /><br />And it dawned on me just about instantly what was going on with Alex and Terrie even though it's not something I've come across frequently. It was something new, but at the same time it was made abundantly clear what was going on with them. Some might think under the circumstances Toby's judgment was clouded, but I think that's just a cop-out. She should have figured it out, it wasn't that hard.<br /><br />The third thing, exactly why the killings were going on did elude me until the end, but I think that's only because it was so far-fetched and not something you'd expect in faerie-land. I don't mind being surprised though, I wish I <i>had</i> been for the whole novel and not just the last 20 pages or so.<br /><br />Now, the part about it being bloated. This book is just chock-full of repetition; Toby getting lost, Toby remarking about how the scenery is different when she looks out the windows, Toby saying how the knowe changes at its whim, Toby drinking coffee, Toby telling people to stick together, people not listening, Gordan bitching Quentin and/or Toby out, Toby drinking more coffee, Quentin wanting to grow up and stay and help, Toby wanting Quentin to grow up but leave and be safe, Toby trying to figure out the murders while more people die, Toby hurting herself, Toby drinking even <i>more</i> coffee (why doesn't this girl have to run to the bathroom every second?!?), everyone that's left getting mad that Toby hasn't figured anything out yet, the cats congregating on the lawn ... lather, rinse, repeat. <b>I honestly think over 100 pages of this monotony could have been cut to streamline the story better.</b><br /><br />ARGH. I'm so frustrated with this book. This one made me so mad that I'm questioning whether I really liked the first one as much as I thought I did. I didn't even like Toby at all in this one but at the same time I really didn't even get a feel for her character, she was running around so much and missing clues while her personality was never really developed that well. <b>She seemed so flat and disconnected that I didn't really care what happened to her.</b> Strangely enough, the only character that I even had any emotion for was Sylvester and I think he's maybe present for all of 10 pages. <br /><br />I'm not really looking forward to the next book like I was looking forward to this one after reading Rosemary and Rue. <b>I was really hoping this one would be great but it turns out it's been a sophomore slump.</b> I will buy the third book, because I'm guessing we'll find out more about her mother and that's something I've been curious about, but <b>I'm not going to be running to the book store on its release date that's for sure.</b><br /><br />Check out my review for books one and three in this series: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/54207257" rel="nofollow noopener">Rosemary and Rue</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/69521042" rel="nofollow noopener">An Artificial Night</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5750317582480212689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_103534938" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103534938" />
    <a title="r." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1283231-r"><img alt="r." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376350955p2/1283231.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103534938?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="r." class="user" itemprop="url" name="r." href="/user/show/1283231-r">r.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283231-r?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1283231-r?shelf=publication-contemporary">publication-contemporary</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103534938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16003875668376145316">Holy crap, this book was SO FRUSTRATING.<br/><br/>Okay, so Toby is clearly the worst detective in the entire world. Every single mystery was easily solved a quarter of the way through the book, but she spends the entire book meandering around, refusing to suspect THE MOST OBVIOUS SUSPECT, and ultimately triumphing through the process of elimination after almost everyone she came there to save has been murdered.<br/><br/>Uh...good job?!?!<br/><br/>But the thing that I find most frustrating is that Toby is supposed to be so cy</span>
  <span id="freeText16003875668376145316" style="display:none">Holy crap, this book was SO FRUSTRATING.<br /><br />Okay, so Toby is clearly the worst detective in the entire world. Every single mystery was easily solved a quarter of the way through the book, but she spends the entire book meandering around, refusing to suspect THE MOST OBVIOUS SUSPECT, and ultimately triumphing through the process of elimination after almost everyone she came there to save has been murdered.<br /><br />Uh...good job?!?!<br /><br />But the thing that I find most frustrating is that Toby is supposed to be so cynical and world-weary, yet she seems to have ZERO UNDERSTANDING of people. Why do I think that? One very important reason: despite it being BLAZINGLY OBVIOUS since literally the FIRST SCENE in which he ever appeared in the first book, Toby somehow still has not managed to even SUSPECT that Tybalt is completely in love with her.<br /><br />Dude appears to spend 95% of his time prowling around her, pulling her pigtails, being HIGHLY protective, possessive, and concerned about her safety, and clutching her to himself when she is injured (which she is a LOT). He carries her home when she is drunk and puts her to bed! He pleads desperately for her to not be dead as she passes in and out of consciousness from her injuries! She has heard his LITERAL ACTUAL THOUGHTS about how after being lost for so long she had finally come back ~to him~. And yet! YET! She persists in believing this fiction that he dislikes her--that theirs is a relationship of mutual enmity.<br /><br />Does he actually need to RUB UP AGAINST HER AND PURR?! You know, in humanoid form SINCE HE HAS ALREADY DONE THIS IN CAT FORM.<br /><br />(For her part, she spends an inordinate amount of time checking him out in his tight pants, pondering his VIRILITY AND MASCULINITY, and spends the entire second book wearing his jacket and noting continuously how it smells like him. So apparently it is not just other people she's terrible at reading.)<br /><br />I hate to break it to you, Toby, but TYBALT WANTS TO LOVE YOU GENTLY WITH HIS BODY, OKAY? HE WANTS TO LOVE YOU ALL NIGHT LONG, GIRL.<br /><br />GET WITH THE PROGRAM.<br /><br />What with the CONSTANT reinforcement of this entire subplot, I can only guess that the author is building up to a REALIZATION/REVEAL but the problem is his interest and her "subconscious" reciprocal feelings are so HAM-FISTED and BLATANT that you are left to wonder how socially inept or just plain stupid she has to be have never so much as NOTICED this. And the fact that it is in first person means that WE KNOW she has somehow never noticed.<br /><br />Listen, I'm not even saying she has to jump the guy. I mean, I'd hit it! But whatever. I'm just saying she needs to be LESS ABSURDLY OBLIVIOUS. ACCEPT THAT HE HAS MORE THAN ANTAGONISTIC FEELINGS TOWARDS HER. It stretches credulity far past the breaking point!<br /><br />Man, whatever. 2.5 stars since this has at least succeeded in FRUSTRATING me enough to make me care.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16003875668376145316" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1672266113" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1672266113" />
    <a title="Alp" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26653561-alp"><img alt="Alp" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462791280p2/26653561.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1672266113?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alp" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alp" href="/user/show/26653561-alp">Alp</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/7884731-a-local-habitation">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1672266113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13294125961486927508">The first half : 4 stars<br/>The second half : 2 stars<br/><br/>I enjoyed the first 50% of the book a lot and I thought it was really better than the first installment in this series. But then the rest of the book proved me otherwise. It didn't impress me as much as I expected. Toby still made numerous bad decisions, which totally ticked me off. I have to admit, I haven’t quite warmed up to her yet, but I trust my GR friends that she will gradually get better. Hopefully, it will happen real soon!<br/><br/>In this book, </span>
  <span id="freeText13294125961486927508" style="display:none">The first half : 4 stars<br />The second half : 2 stars<br /><br />I enjoyed the first 50% of the book a lot and I thought it was really better than the first installment in this series. But then the rest of the book proved me otherwise. It didn't impress me as much as I expected. Toby still made numerous bad decisions, which totally ticked me off. I have to admit, I haven’t quite warmed up to her yet, but I trust my GR friends that she will gradually get better. Hopefully, it will happen real soon!<br /><br />In this book, I had a couple of issues with Toby.<br /><br />Firstly, since she nearly died from being a mobile punching bag in Rosemary and Rue, I supposed she should develop her fighting skills in this book. But no, she still hasn’t known how to fight at all. Why on earth didn't she get some more practice, or learn martial arts, or take a self-defense class, or whatever useful for her job? Evidently, she has shown no ability to protect herself when facing dangerous situations.<br /><br />Secondly, as Knight of Shadowed hills, why doesn’t Toby have any suitable weapons? Fortunately, in this story she prepared her own weapons, the baseball bat (seriously? I suggest that she should bring along the golf iron because it’s longer and more noticeable.) and the knife which a girl in the first book gave her. But unfortunately, she never had a chance to use them to defend herself. Instead, she used the knife to cut herself twice and almost bled to death! (She said she didn't intend to cut too deep, and oops, it was the silver knife! How could she know that? Gah!)<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“You were bleeding so much we didn’t dare move you,” said Elliot. “If Tybalt hadn’t told us you did it to yourself, we’d have thought you were attacked. I’ve never met anyone who cuts themselves open as often as you do.”<br />“It’s a talent of hers,” said Tybalt.</i>
</b><br /><br />I couldn’t agree more!<br /><br />The funniest thing was that she asked Quentin if he had any weapons and when he told her he had none, she asked him what they were teaching him. After a few stunned seconds, I laughed out loud eventually! How dare she ask him this question? It was generous of him not to ask her back this same thing!<br /><br />And finally, she always believes she has to protect everyone, which in fact, she can’t even protect herself. She has very little fighting instinct but she acted as if she was the leader. When the bad guy tried to kill her, she thought she was going to die then she gave up. How heroic! Why didn’t she fight back until her last breath? <br />*Shakes head in utter disappointment*<br /><br />Some parts in this book seemed off but I successfully ignored them. Good thing I did because the story was mostly entertaining. There was a good plot twist and a nice ending. Moreover, Tybalt has grown on me though I still don’t know him very well.<br /><br />Do I want to read the next book? Of course, I definitely want to continue with the series. I haven’t given up on Toby yet.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13294125961486927508" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6416510985941993880">The land of Faerie has always intermingled with the mortal world. With their secret Courts. Terrifying creatures and legends. Where their <b> beauty is only equal to their danger. </b> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454937429ra/18031337.gif' width='170' height='150' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>One definitely unique change to the fey world is that changelings aren't stolen children like most fey stories, instead they are mortal halfbreeds who don't quite fit into either worlds. <b>Enter our heroine, October 'Toby' Daye.</b> And all the shenanigans she gets into. <br/><br/>Re-Reading this series I'm able to appreciate and enjoy</span>
  <span id="freeText6416510985941993880" style="display:none">The land of Faerie has always intermingled with the mortal world. With their secret Courts. Terrifying creatures and legends. Where their <b> beauty is only equal to their danger. </b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454937429ra/18031337.gif" width="170" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>One definitely unique change to the fey world is that changelings aren't stolen children like most fey stories, instead they are mortal halfbreeds who don't quite fit into either worlds. <b>Enter our heroine, October 'Toby' Daye.</b> And all the shenanigans she gets into. <br><br>Re-Reading this series I'm able to appreciate and enjoy it a lot more than the first go-around. <br><br>Now that I know what the world is like, see where all of this is going with Toby Daye and Tybalt, know what's up with all of the cryptic references to her past, and recognize which characters are actually important staples in this universe in later books <br><br>So let me summarize: <br><br><b>
  <u>Book 1</u>
</b>: Good intro book, general set-up <br><b>
  <u>Book 2</u>
</b>: Established world better and I fell in love with Tybalt <br><b>
  <u>Book 3</u>
</b>: intro the series plot of the series with the Firsts<br><b>
  <u>Book 4</u>
</b>: little bland and dry <br><b>
  <u>Book 5</u>
</b>: depressing as fuuuck <br><b>
  <u>Book 6</u>
</b>: Toby back in action! The banter coming back, and group dynamic forming <br><b>
  <u>Book 7</u>
</b>: *Top fucking tier!* <br><b>
  <u>Book 8</u>
</b>: We have a system and I’m liking it <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1602093215ra/30205524.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I definitely plan to be continuing this series and recommend it as an entertaining series. Each book in itself is enjoyable, but the power definitely lies in the series as a whole and just how creative this world is.<b> Highly recommend giving it a try if you like <u>fey, fun &amp; mystery</u>. See if it's your cup of tea.</b></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1471647669?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1471647669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4203734297074360387"><b>*** 3.65 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with the UF addicts at BB&B! </b><br/><br/>The second of an Urban Fantasy series about a half Fae, Half human PI who solves mysteries for a Fae ruler. Since it is the second in a running series, it was easier to get into, because we already had October's background, knew some parts of the world, and most of all, got to love some of the characters. Toby was much more comfortable in her skin and the whole story felt much more three dimensional than the previous one, which cemented my de</span>
  <span id="freeText4203734297074360387" style="display:none"><b>*** 3.65 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with the UF addicts at BB&amp;B! </b><br /><br />The second of an Urban Fantasy series about a half Fae, Half human PI who solves mysteries for a Fae ruler. Since it is the second in a running series, it was easier to get into, because we already had October's background, knew some parts of the world, and most of all, got to love some of the characters. Toby was much more comfortable in her skin and the whole story felt much more three dimensional than the previous one, which cemented my decision to follow the series through its complete course. Also, I love cats and cranky old people, so my enjoyment was guarantied:):):)<br /><br />The issues I had this time were with the plot... It had a lot of potential, but somehow did not fit my own personal expectations... This makes no less a good book, it just let me a bit down as to the direction of the story. However, none of the plot lowered my enjoyment of the characters themselves. They are charming, lovable and you can not help but feel for all of them. The range of paranormal species continues growing and the world building is absolutely fascinating! We get to delve even deeper into the Fae mythology and how this different, magical world could be interpreted by modern technology... Interesting and sad at the same time... <br /><br /><i>"We were told we will live forever, that promise has been betrayed...!!! "</i> *heart brakes slowly...* ... <i>"But there is hope...!"</i><br /><br />This book had a melancholy feel to it, but it had hilarious parts and it kept me engaged throughout! I would recommend it to all Urban Fantasy lovers of all ages, but make sure you start from book one for full understanding and more comprehensive enjoyment:):):) <br /><br />To all of you, I wish happy reading and many good books! :-)<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

  <span id="freeText16727068696027678729" style="display:none">A Local Habitation (October Daye #2), Seanan McGuire<br /><br />October "Toby" Daye is a changeling, the daughter of Amandine of the fae and a mortal man. Like her mother, she is gifted in blood magic, able to read what has happened to a person through a mere taste of blood. <br /><br />Toby is the only changeling who has earned knighthood, and she re-earns that position every day, undertaking assignments for her liege, Sylvester, the Duke of the Shadowed Hills.<br /><br />Now Sylvester has asked her to go to the County of Tamed Lightning—otherwise known as Fremont, CA—to make sure that all is well with his niece, Countess January O'Leary, whom he has not been able to contact. <br /><br />It seems like a simple enough assignment—but when dealing with the realm of Faerie nothing is ever as simple as it seems. Toby soon discovers that someone has begun murdering people close to January, whose domain is a buffer between Sylvester's realm and a scheming rival duchy. If Toby can't find the killer soon, she may well become the next victim. <br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش روز شانزدهم ماه فوریه سال 2017 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: سکونت محلی: کتاب دوم از سری اکتبر دای؛ نویسنده: سینان مک گوایر؛<br /><br />سیلوستر نگران خواهرزاده خود در ژانویه است زیرا او به تماسهای وی پاسخ نمیدهد. ژانویه میگوید سیلوستر جواب نمیدهد. به وضوح خطوط تلفن هک میشوند، در حالی که توبی میداند که خطوط تلفن خارج خوب کار میکنند. ...؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_137837568" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137837568" />
    <a title="The Flooze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/355739-the-flooze"><img alt="The Flooze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599955192p2/355739.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137837568?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Flooze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Flooze" href="/user/show/355739-the-flooze">The Flooze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=urban-fantasy-paranormal">urban-fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=vanquished_2011">vanquished_2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=glutton_for_punishment">glutton_for_punishment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137837568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2153694721651518132">ETA: I've continued reading this series and want to point out I gave books four and five considerably higher ratings. Four stars each. <br/>_________________________<br/><br/><br/>** <i>Almost</i> a 3 **<br/><br/>Seanan McGuire is talented. She’s just useless at crafting mysteries.<br/><br/>Unlike the first book, <i>A Local Habitation</i> resulted in me liking Toby. She is strong-minded and determined. She’s also quite amusing in her interactions, particularly when conversing with Quentin or Tybalt. She’s fiercely loyal, holds duty in high regard, </span>
  <span id="freeText2153694721651518132" style="display:none">ETA: I've continued reading this series and want to point out I gave books four and five considerably higher ratings. Four stars each. <br />_________________________<br /><br /><br />** <i>Almost</i> a 3 **<br /><br />Seanan McGuire is talented. She’s just useless at crafting mysteries.<br /><br />Unlike the first book, <i>A Local Habitation</i> resulted in me liking Toby. She is strong-minded and determined. She’s also quite amusing in her interactions, particularly when conversing with Quentin or Tybalt. She’s fiercely loyal, holds duty in high regard, and cares deeply for her friends.<br /><br />That said, she’s a terrible investigator. Most of this book takes place on one compound, and yet Toby is still running from place to place, finding more bodies than clues, and frequently damaging herself in the process. It’s almost comical. When she does come across a clue, she seems to dismiss examining it further. She’s always allowing something else to take precedence rather than stopping to think things over. Her investigation includes little more than sifting through paperwork and conducting a few spells. It’s tiresome, watching people get killed while perfectly good hints go to waste. At the end, the case is solved primarily through the process of elimination. No wit, no intuition necessary. <br /><br />And yet I admit McGuire has talent. Her skill at world-building is evident, as showcased in her manipulation of fae lore to create a believable, varied cast of characters and an understandable magic system. She is adept at humorous dialogue, made clear by the opening scenes between drunken Toby and sober Tybalt. So I’m not sure why she fails so spectacularly at weaving together plot threads to form an intriguing mystery. I want so much to like these books, but the investigations are so haphazard and pointless that it’s hard to be satisfied. Toby is supposed to be a professional PI, but apart from her skill with blood magic she lacks the necessary tools to solve anything. While I might like her as a friend, I certainly wouldn’t assign her any work.<br /><br />Liking October Daye and the rest of the characters, I’m willing to read the next book. However, I don’t know how long I’ll stick with this series unless there’s a marked improvement in Toby’s sleuthing. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2153694721651518132" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1574385602" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1574385602" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14323468-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434090906p2/14323468.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1574385602?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/14323468-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jo by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=mine">mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=book-boyfriend">book-boyfriend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=gr2016">gr2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1574385602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer761314581957280999"><p>16/03/2016 Buddy read with my fellow UF addicts over at BB&B, because this series is <b>really</b> good!</p> <blockquote>
  <i>"My mother was so strong she could taste the death of plants. She could never stomach maple syrup; she said it tasted like trees screaming.” </i>
</blockquote> <p>Toby is half-human, half-Daoine Sidhe. The Daoine Sidhe is known as the blood-workers of the Fae. Because she is the daughter of the greatest blood-worker alive, Amandine, she’s now slouch when it comes to blood magic. She’s able to ride the blood, gaining</p></span>
  <span id="freeText761314581957280999" style="display:none"><p>16/03/2016 Buddy read with my fellow UF addicts over at BB&amp;B, because this series is <b>really</b> good!</p> <blockquote>
  <i>"My mother was so strong she could taste the death of plants. She could never stomach maple syrup; she said it tasted like trees screaming.” </i>
</blockquote> <p>Toby is half-human, half-Daoine Sidhe. The Daoine Sidhe is known as the blood-workers of the Fae. Because she is the daughter of the greatest blood-worker alive, Amandine, she’s now slouch when it comes to blood magic. She’s able to ride the blood, gaining access to the person’s memories seeing what had happened to them right before. And she is asked by her liege, Sylvester, the Duke of the Shadowed Hills to investigate into the welfare of his niece, Countess January O’Leary, whom he has been unable to contact.</p> <p>And upon arrival, Toby and her assistant Quentin, soon discovers that things aren’t what they seem, and that someone has been killing the people that works with January. And now Toby needs to find the killer before she fails at another task Sylvester has given her. </p> <p>I love the fact that the fantasy aspect is mixed so well with a mystery/suspense, it just makes this part of my all-time favorite UF series’!! With every instalment you have a new mystery to solve, and for someone like me who loves a good puzzle, this is just excellent. Also there is the continuous mystery of what happened to Toby 14 years ago. And I cannot wait to learn more about that.</p><blockquote>
  <i>"I stumble and fall, and I always get up and keep going. That’s what it means to be a changeling.” </i>
</blockquote> <p>That in a nutshell is Toby. No matter how many times her life is in danger, or how disastrous a situation seems, or how many times she fails, she doesn’t give up, and that I love about her.</p> <blockquote>
  <i> “Oh.” Her disappointment was briefly audible before she covered it with briskness, saying, “Well, good. I can get some things done without needing to worry about your happy ass showing up.” </i>
</blockquote> <p>This series has such excellent secondary characters, like the Luidaeg. Who is the Firstborn, and very cranky, but lovable because of it. I also love Quentin, who is Toby’s apprentice in this book. He’s so sweet and I hope he will be a permanent fixture in this series. </p><blockquote>
  <i>Three heads of roughly the same size and shape poked over the back of the couch as I approached. Two were brown and cream, belonging to my half- Siamese cats, Cagney and Lacey. The third was gray-green and thorny, and belonged to Spike, the resident rose goblin.<br />“Morning,” I said. The cats withdrew while Spike scrabbled fully into view, rattling its thorns in enthusiastic greeting. Adorable, if weird. </i>
</blockquote> <p>One of my favorite characters, Spike (second only to Tybalt ;-)), the rose goblin is now a permanent addition to Toby’s home (because she named him ;-)) and all I can say … again… is:: I WANT ONE!!! </p><p> </p><p>I really enjoyed this book. And the fact that with each book I learn more of the Fae lore. And I LOVE this world the author created and the way she writes!!! It’s fascinating and captivating and so interesting that my mind is blown away, and I'm just in awe. </p><p> </p><blockquote>
  <i>If you don’t mind my asking, when was your last shower?” I stared at him. Quentin’s mouth dropped open, and he sputtered, “How . . . how can you . . .” “Relax, relax!” Elliot laughed, holding up his hands. “You just look a bit frayed around the edges. May I clean you?” “What . . . oh,” I said, catching on. The Bannick are bath-spirits; they’re obsessed with cleanliness, and Faerie being what it is, they can sometimes enforce their own ideas about hygiene. Nothing cleans a person like a Bannick. “Sure.” </i>
</blockquote> <p>I especially found the mention and description of the bath-spirit fabulous. I think I need one for myself. In case of emergency:-D</p><p> </p><p>And finally we learn more about the night-haunts. When the Fae die, they can’t leave bodies behind that might give away their existence to the human world. Especially because they don’t decay. So the nigh-haunts carry the bodies away, and in their place is left mannequins that are made to look real to the human eye. So fascinating right?? I love it. </p><p> </p><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You are truly endearing when you sleep. I attribute this to the exotic nature of seeing you in a state of silence.<br />—Tybalt</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <p>And of course sexy Tybalt made an appearance. I just love the banter between Toby and Tybalt. It is hilarious and wonderful. And I REALLY hope that there will be romance between these two soon. I need my romance and Tybalt fix. </p><p> This is a wonderful series. Right up there with the other best UF series’ like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38619.Magic_Bites" rel="nofollow noopener"> Kate Daniels </a>,<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/71811.Moon_Called" rel="nofollow noopener"> Mercy Thompson </a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2355575.Cry_Wolf" rel="nofollow noopener"> Alpha &amp; Omega </a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6329547-on-the-edge" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Edge series </a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1421990.Halfway_to_the_Grave?from_new_nav=true&amp;ac=1&amp;from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener"> Night Huntress </a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7039218-once-burned" rel="nofollow noopener"> Night Prince </a>. And a must read for all who loves this genre. </p><p>
  <br />
</p></span>

<div id="review_198362172" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198362172" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/198362172?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">folklore fans, fans of UF, those wanting a light read</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=female-lead">female-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=supernatural-mystery">supernatural-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198362172" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1244199160711427286"><br/>The second installment of the urban fantasy October Daye series, A Local Habitation was initially an improvement on Rosemary and Rue, especially due to the integration of unusual beings from folklore–the Bannick cleaning scene was a fun interpretation of cleaning fairies, and the hippocampi fish tank was clever. (Aside-I would dearly love a little Spike of my own). The opening scene with an inebriated October escorting her almost equally inebriated friends to the train was fun, and dialogue with</span>
  <span id="freeText1244199160711427286" style="display:none"><br />The second installment of the urban fantasy October Daye series, A Local Habitation was initially an improvement on Rosemary and Rue, especially due to the integration of unusual beings from folklore–the Bannick cleaning scene was a fun interpretation of cleaning fairies, and the hippocampi fish tank was clever. (Aside-I would dearly love a little Spike of my own). The opening scene with an inebriated October escorting her almost equally inebriated friends to the train was fun, and dialogue with Tybalt well-written–a little bit flirty, but without all those smoldering glances and peering through eyelashes that show up in less well-written UF. I liked the Luidaeg, even if her and October’s dialogue did start to remind me of Wesley and the Dread Pirate Roberts. The demonstration of October’s skills and the nighthaunt background was very interesting, and well done, with that eerie touch of folklore menace (fae are not nice, after all). Certainly, McGuire has a gift for character creation and dialogue.<br /><br />October spends a lot of time running around a maze-like converted warehouse with people dying around her–after awhile, I started to wonder if I was reading a Scream script, since it lacked the horror of a truly suspenseful setting. There’s a brief acknowledgement of this when she orders everyone to stay in groups of two for “safety,” but then promptly lets some of them run off or go do some crucial job by themselves. [ Needless to say, they died, except for the killer. (hide spoiler)] The teen mock-horror flick connection comes particularly clear when the entrance gates fall on her car as they are returning, presumably preventing her from ever leaving the estate again. <br /><br /><br />***************************<br /><br />Full review posted at:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2014/09/03/a-local-habitation-by-seanan-mcguire/">https://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2014/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1244199160711427286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4989092954467255018">I was not a fan of the first book, I didn't hate it I just didn't love it but after being told that it gets better I picked this one up. I wasn't Disappointed. <br/><br/>After being asked by her liege, Toby was set on to The Tamed Lightning a.k.a Fremont, CA with her charge and friend Quentin.   <span id="freeText4989092954467255018" style="display:none">I was not a fan of the first book, I didn't hate it I just didn't love it but after being told that it gets better I picked this one up. I wasn't Disappointed. <br><br>After being asked by her liege, Toby was set on to The Tamed Lightning a.k.a Fremont, CA with her charge and friend Quentin. Sylvester asked her to check on his niece January. What she finds are mystery and mayhem. A lot of wit from herself and Quentin and yes some cats.... a lot of cats..... <br><br>She sticks around to help January and her crew. She stumbles on something big and she gets herself into trouble. I love so much about this book. So much made me question and shake my head just a little bit.. oh yeah. There is also Tybalt. Not enough to make me a happy girl but he was there. I love that Cat he makes me snicker. I think there is something coming for him and Toby I just can't wait to see if I am right. totally worth a read. Maybe a second if I find myself in dire need of a little mystery and a little bit of Tybalt....<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380907728ra/3169431.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_965312276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/965312276" />
    <a title="Maria Dimitrova" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova"><img alt="Maria Dimitrova" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563534668p2/15922517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/965312276?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Dimitrova" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Dimitrova" href="/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova">Maria Dimitrova</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=br-bbb-2016">br-bbb-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=october-daye">october-daye</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=br-bbb">br-bbb</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer965312276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6881297319963097785"><b> Buddy read with the UF lovers from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164' rel='nofollow noopener'>BB&B</a></b> <br/><br/>The second instalment of the October Daye series takes us deeper into the Fae world when Toby is sent to investigate the sudden lack of communication from the neighbouring County - Tamed Lightning under the regency of Sylvester's niece - January. So with this book we got two more month named characters - January (Jan) and April. We've got 9 more free names for new characters ;p Seriously the Fae seem obsessed with months :D Back to the plot, Toby is sent </span>
  <span id="freeText6881297319963097785" style="display:none"><b> Buddy read with the UF lovers from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164" rel="nofollow noopener">BB&amp;B</a></b> <br /><br />The second instalment of the October Daye series takes us deeper into the Fae world when Toby is sent to investigate the sudden lack of communication from the neighbouring County - Tamed Lightning under the regency of Sylvester's niece - January. So with this book we got two more month named characters - January (Jan) and April. We've got 9 more free names for new characters ;p Seriously the Fae seem obsessed with months :D Back to the plot, Toby is sent there with just Quentin as back up (as if a teenage boy can be that much of a help) because of the political aspects. Basically the County is a buffer zone between Sylvester's Duchy and the Duchy of Dreaming Glass and they're on the brink of war. Apparently Fae view war as a sport. When Toby arrives at ALH - the location of the knowe in the mortal world she faces mistrust and outright paranoia. And the denizens of Tamed Lightning have a good reason for it - they are dying one at a time under mysterious circumstances. And it's up to Toby to figure out who the killer is.<br /><br />This book wasn't as depressing as the first one. Sure there was a lot more death but it wasn't as personal so it didn't hit me as hard as the event in the previous one. Toby's a lot more confident but also has a chip on her shoulder and is more careful with the people that depend on her. It's obvious how hard Dare's death has affected her. And that's a good thing because Toby's reckless. She knows she's not immortal or powerful as the purebloods but she still pushes herself harder than any pureblood would ever do. Kudos to Quentin for not abandoning her at the first sign of trouble even after Toby insisted on him getting back to safety. Toby's guilt over the imprisonment of Luna and Raysel makes her almost suicidal in her attempts to not let Sylvester down again. Even though he'll never hold her responsible for failing as long as she's done everything in her power to succeed. Guilt and fear are two very powerful emotions that have the common ability to make us not think rationally. Thankfully Toby has good people around her to help her when she overextends herself and maybe one day she'll work over her issues. <br /><br />I loved Tybalt's involvement. This time he appears early on and plays the knight in shinning armour to a very drunk Toby. There are definitely sparks of attraction between those two. But Toby being oblivious to it and Tybalt acting like the cat he is I don't think we'll see them as a couple any time soon. I hope I'm wrong about that cause I really ship them :D They make such a great team as seen in this book after Tybalt shows in Tamed Lightning under the excuse of the dead Queen of Cats. Toby's naive enough to fall for that but the way he reacts to her injuries tells a different story. And I remember the little snippet of his thoughts from the previous book when Toby rode his blood. <br /><br />The murder investigation was extremely frustrating. We had a limited pool of suspects and even when they started to drop off like flies I couldn't figure out who the killer is until the very end. They all had an alibi or a close person who was dead so it didn't make sense. Except it did. And in hindsight I feel like a total moron for not figuring it out! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Why oh why did I assume that it's one killer? Or that it has to be done out of hate? It made perfect sense for Gordon and April to work together but I'm too used to "one book = one major bad guy" to even consider the possibility of two killers. I'm ashamed of myself.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The reasons behind the murders were bizarre. I mean haven't these guys watched any film about the robots' revolution or AI taking over the world. Or pretty much any other sci-fi dealing with similar themes. Was Battlestar Galactica out when this book was written? In the end they paid the ultimate price but at least they could say they did it for the good of Fairy. If that can help the survivors sleep at night. <br /><br />Toby pulled out some major magic tricks in this book and I'm wondering if she's not more powerful than she thinks or maybe there's some permanent change from her handling the hope chest from the previous book. The way Tybalt reacted to some of the things she pulled tells me she's not supposed to be able to do that. Or maybe he just doesn't know what she's supposed to be capable of. The different breeds of Fae seem to be very secretive of some of their power. It does bring up interesting questions and possibilities to be explored in the rest of the series. And I'm so looking forward to diving deeper into Toby's world. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6881297319963097785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
