    <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller"><img alt="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517553177p2/13396599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3467442609?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller">Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3467442609" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16546365873373183540">I’m going to need some encouragement to keep reading this series.<br/><br/>I really want to like it, but I’m struggling. The first book was a bit mediocre (something I don’t hold against introductory UF novels), but had a lot of promise. I was expecting this second book to show some improvements, but ended up liking it less.<br/><br/>First off, the storyline didn’t have anything to do with what happened in the first novel. October was sent off on a tangent mission that, from my initial impression, had absolutely no</span>
  <span id="freeText16546365873373183540" style="display:none">I’m going to need some encouragement to keep reading this series.<br><br>I really want to like it, but I’m struggling. The first book was a bit mediocre (something I don’t hold against introductory UF novels), but had a lot of promise. I was expecting this second book to show some improvements, but ended up liking it less.<br><br>First off, the storyline didn’t have anything to do with what happened in the first novel. October was sent off on a tangent mission that, from my initial impression, had absolutely nothing to do with the main trajectory of the series. It lost the sense of momentum I was hoping it would nurture.<br><br>A tangent in itself wouldn’t have necessarily been a bad thing, but unfortunately I thought it was an incredibly <i>boring</i> tangent. Mostly due to its predictability.<br><br>If I, as the reader, have exactly the same amount of information as the main POV character, I should NOT be able to reason out who the killer is almost half a novel before said character figures it out for herself. The mystery was excruciating long-winded. I even accidentally skipped ahead several chapters and, after flipping back, realized I hadn’t missed much at all. And to make matters worse, there were multiple things the character remained oblivious about for the sake of plot extension, which did not endear me to her sustainability as a leading lady.<br><br>BUT… I still don’t absolutely hate it. I like October’s general personality and am really interested in all of the side characters. I like the framework for the world. And I like the small ideas throughout that set this series slightly apart from all the other UFs I’ve read. I think that’s why I’m willing to field conversations to convince me to keep reading. After all, I almost abandoned Kate Daniels at the first book, and now I’m an IA superfan. Series turnarounds happen, especially within the first few books.<br><br>Series status: I have the third book already and am planning to read it. However, I don’t have access to free copies from my library for the rest of the series, so it’s going to take some serious persuasion to get me to invest almost $10 per book going forward. I’m hoping for some spoiler-free endorsements from all my fellow UF addicts. :)<br><br>Recommendations: at this point, <i>I’m</i> the one looking for recommendations on whether or not this series is worth continuing. So far the first book was mediocre and this one was an even bigger let down… but both offer enough promise to keep me from abandoning it outright. Please help. :)<br><br>Via The Obsessive Bookseller at <a href="https://www.NikiHawkes.com" rel="nofollow noopener">www.NikiHawkes.com</a><br><br>Other books you might like:<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2754510.Storm_Born__Dark_Swan__1_" title="Storm Born (Dark Swan #1) by Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1327900947l/2754510._SY75_.jpg" alt="Storm Born (Dark Swan #1) by Richelle Mead" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3588137.Blue_Diablo__Corine_Solomon___1_" title="Blue Diablo (Corine Solomon, #1) by Ann Aguirre" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1304756284l/3588137._SY75_.jpg" alt="Blue Diablo (Corine Solomon, #1) by Ann Aguirre" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6329547.On_the_Edge__The_Edge___1_" title="On the Edge (The Edge, #1) by Ilona Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_3286335626" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3286335626" />
    <a title="Hollis " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16668577-hollis"><img alt="Hollis " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586714618p2/16668577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3286335626?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hollis " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hollis " href="/user/show/16668577-hollis">Hollis </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=baa-baa-black-sheep">baa-baa-black-sheep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=book-buddy-recs">book-buddy-recs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=chick-is-clueless-because-plot">chick-is-clueless-because-plot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=family-focused">family-focused</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=finished-in-april-2020">finished-in-april-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16668577-hollis?shelf=grief-or-loss">grief-or-loss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3286335626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7966242763843325991">S t r u g g l e b u s.<br/><br/>That's what this whole read was. It's a good thing I was warned in advance that this book would not be a favourite and would require some pushing through because oh boy was <b>that</b> accurate. So I'm paying it forward and passing along that warning.<br/><br/>Some of what I expressed as my main issue with book one was definitely present in book two. More romantic entanglements (because why not), more making things complicated with the existing ones (because why not), and combined with a my</span>
  <span id="freeText7966242763843325991" style="display:none">S t r u g g l e b u s.<br /><br />That's what this whole read was. It's a good thing I was warned in advance that this book would not be a favourite and would require some pushing through because oh boy was <b>that</b> accurate. So I'm paying it forward and passing along that warning.<br /><br />Some of what I expressed as my main issue with book one was definitely present in book two. More romantic entanglements (because why not), more making things complicated with the existing ones (because why not), and combined with a mystery that I felt was just dragged out (because.. you get it), made worse by so much information being kept away from the MC and her investigative buddy (..), and compounded by an element I'm sure was supposed to be a surprise regarding a certain character, but wasn't because duh it's obvious and I've seen it before, just.. overall? Not a good time.<br /><br />Don't even get me started on the appearance of a certain line that is iconic for the <i>Kate Daniels</i> world showing up in this one. Multiple times. Sure, it's not owned by IA, nor is it an unusual thing to say, but still. Grr arg. I was even trying not to compare anymore and then <b>that</b> happened. Not my fault.<br /><br />October as an MC failed to impress me, I wasn't loving the romance (as mentioned above and also because this didn't further my ship), the mystery was annoying, and this is also the second book where October is being blamed for things that have nothing to do with her? This better not be a trend. One of the characters kidnapped in book one literaly blames October for it, even though she didn't do the act, and was also disappeated for over a decade because she was trying to help, and in this one? Same thing. Suspicion, blame, distrust, like.. constantly. So annoying.<br /><br />Also annoying? October tells everyone to pair up, no one should be alone, due to killer on the loose. Right after, everyone spends at least some time on their own; when confronted by the fact that they aren't following orders, and they explain why, even though all the reasons are dumb, October accepts it. Then October is alone multiple times. Other people are alone. Again. She bitches them out. Then suddenly she's alone again and only then realizes she's a hypocrite. Eye twitch. And this was only one example of just some of the dumb ridiculous trudgery. <br /><br />Another being.. why was there so much crying? <br /><br />I'm no stranger to McGuire's books, though obviously not this series, and I'm surprised how.. not great the writing is? Was this her first few books? I should look into that.<br /><br />So, yes, not a favourite, though not surprised due to advance warning (even though, yes, surprised by just how <b>much</b> I disliked it), and holding out hope book three lives up to all the hype it was getting in my group chat. Thanks, again, buddies for the support. I really needed it for this book. If this had been book one, this would've been as far as I went. Probably, maybe. It would've been a “might pick this up again later..” aka never situation. But we shall push on.<br /><br />1.5 stars <br /><br />---<br /><br />This review can also be found at <a href="https://atakefromtwocities.home.blog/2020/04/24/a-local-habitation-by-seanan-mcguire/" rel="nofollow noopener">A Take From Two Cities</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7966242763843325991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2693292383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13015369168182353121">I enjoyed this book, but not quite as much as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6294549.Rosemary_and_Rue__October_Daye___1_' title='Rosemary and Rue (October Daye, #1) by Seanan McGuire' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rosemary and Rue</a>. McGuire's writing style is still top-notch, but this one felt like it dragged a bit, as though there wasn't <i>quite</i> enough story to justify the length. And aside from Toby, Quentin, Tybalt, and April, there just weren't any other characters I cared about...this decreased my enjoyment a bit.<br/><br/>But overall, a solid work of UF. There are some additional world-building elements thrown into the mix (one of the author's strengths), and I liked</span>
  <span id="freeText13015369168182353121" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book, but not quite as much as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6294549.Rosemary_and_Rue__October_Daye___1_" title="Rosemary and Rue (October Daye, #1) by Seanan McGuire" rel="nofollow noopener">Rosemary and Rue</a>. McGuire's writing style is still top-notch, but this one felt like it dragged a bit, as though there wasn't <i>quite</i> enough story to justify the length. And aside from Toby, Quentin, Tybalt, and April, there just weren't any other characters I cared about...this decreased my enjoyment a bit.<br /><br />But overall, a solid work of UF. There are some additional world-building elements thrown into the mix (one of the author's strengths), and I liked seeing Quentin's development as a character throughout the course of the novel.<br /><br />I also like how "normal" (relatively-speaking...) Toby is, which is refreshing compared to reading about over-the-top characters. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2944678559502812901">Reading this was like watching mice in a labyrinth, feeling cruel and amused and betting on that grey little mouse that may look pathetic but you know it's scrappy enough to beat the others. It may be bloody, broken and half dead by the time it reaches the finish line but hey, who said anything about it being easy?<br/><br/>I am honestly intrigued to see what more tricks October has up her sleeve, the latest one was kinda crazy if not entirely unexpected given enough time to think.   <span id="freeText2944678559502812901" style="display:none">Reading this was like watching mice in a labyrinth, feeling cruel and amused and betting on that grey little mouse that may look pathetic but you know it's scrappy enough to beat the others. It may be bloody, broken and half dead by the time it reaches the finish line but hey, who said anything about it being easy?<br /><br />I am honestly intrigued to see what more tricks October has up her sleeve, the latest one was kinda crazy if not entirely unexpected given enough time to think. And judging by Tybalt's reaction there's definitely more where that came from. What does he know?<br /><br />This is shaping up to be one of the coolest series I've read lately and I love the way author goes about the whole "Hero" thing. All things considered, it's grounded and more realistic than most.<br /><br /><i>The hero's journey has suffered in modern years. Once we could've gotten a knight in shining armor riding to the rescue, pennants flying. These days you're lucky to get a battered changeling and her underage, half-trained assistant, and the princesses are confused technological wizards in towers of silicon and steel. Standards aren't what they used to be.</i><br />Over and out</span>

<div id="review_102419650" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102419650" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388694025p2/3344685.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102419650?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-print">books-i-own-print</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=for-review-read">for-review-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-kindle">books-i-own-kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102419650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13606738309545866317">Two books in and I'm already totally hooked on the October Daye series! Toby seemed a lot more settled in this book, she's still dealing with the emotional fallout of events from the first book but she's got past the stay in bed all day wallowing part and now she's more ready to face the world and her friends again. She's back doing what she does best, working as a PI taking on cases for both humans and the fae and she's starting to get her life back on track.<br/><br/><b>A Local Habitation kicks</b> off with he</span>
  <span id="freeText13606738309545866317" style="display:none">Two books in and I'm already totally hooked on the October Daye series! Toby seemed a lot more settled in this book, she's still dealing with the emotional fallout of events from the first book but she's got past the stay in bed all day wallowing part and now she's more ready to face the world and her friends again. She's back doing what she does best, working as a PI taking on cases for both humans and the fae and she's starting to get her life back on track.<br /><br /><b>A Local Habitation kicks</b> off with her liege Sylvester asking Toby to travel to his niece's realm Tamed Lightning to check on her. January normally calls him regularly and he's worried because she's been out of contact for weeks and isn't returning any of his phone calls. It should be a simple job, check out Tamed Lightning and remind January to call her uncle then come straight back home, but when she arrives Toby quickly discovers something suspicious is going on. People in Tamed Lightning have been dying in mysterious circumstances and it is up to Toby to try and figure out exactly what is going on - before she can become one of the victims herself.<br /><br />This series is still pretty dark and watching Toby working her blood magic was disgustingly creepy at times but there seemed to be more lighter moments in this book than the first one. I was really glad that Toby had a new sidekick in trainee Quentin, he's a bit like a younger brother to Toby and adds a lot of humour to the story. We also got to see more of Connor who I like as a character but I'm really hoping doesn't turn into a love interest, he has history with Toby and it looks like he'd be more than willing to pick things up where they left off but he also happens to be married which is a total no go area for me even if his marriage is a political match rather than a love story. My favourite character by far is Tybalt though, he steals the show with every appearance and I have a strong suspicion that he's far more interested in Toby than she realises. I'm totally on board ship Tybalt and I'm hoping his role in the story will continue to increase as the series continues.<br /><br />I don't want to say too much about what is happening in Tamed Lightning but I really enjoyed the way <b>Seanan McGuire</b> has mixed old and new to come up with something completely unique. There were definitely concepts that I've not come across before and I'm really enjoying how she's expanding her world. I had my suspicions about several of the characters and while some of my guesses were partly correct I was never quite able to nail things entirely because of the twists the author threw at us. There was a fascinating scene with the Night Haunts and we're introduced to a few other types of fae in this instalment so I'm enjoying learning about all their different abilities.<br /><br />This series has me totally hooked and I'm planning on diving straight into the next one now I've finished writing this review!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13606738309545866317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer319269937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17611302723200405570">Well, that was terrible.<br/><br/>Firstly, the pacing. McGuire could have had a book a quarter the size of this novel if she had cut out the repetitions. I cannot believe how many times the characters explained to themselves, explained to each other, or explained to us what was going on. Honestly, this was a novel written for adults, not chimps.<br/><br/>Secondly, the characters. Initially, in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6294549.Rosemary_and_Rue__October_Daye___1_' title='Rosemary and Rue (October Daye, #1) by Seanan McGuire' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rosemary and Rue</a>, I didn't fully enjoy October as the main character. She doesn't really have much going for her; she isn't</span>
  <span id="freeText17611302723200405570" style="display:none">Well, that was terrible.<br /><br />Firstly, the pacing. McGuire could have had a book a quarter the size of this novel if she had cut out the repetitions. I cannot believe how many times the characters explained to themselves, explained to each other, or explained to us what was going on. Honestly, this was a novel written for adults, not chimps.<br /><br />Secondly, the characters. Initially, in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6294549.Rosemary_and_Rue__October_Daye___1_" title="Rosemary and Rue (October Daye, #1) by Seanan McGuire" rel="nofollow noopener">Rosemary and Rue</a>, I didn't fully enjoy October as the main character. She doesn't really have much going for her; she isn't all that intelligent, she doesn't have much fae power, and she's not really all that pleasant. You have to give a character more than stubbornness bordering on the ridiculous. However, as we got to know her she had a sort of street-kid charm, in that she was tough but vulnerable and the moments when she <i>did</i> let herself care were actually sweet. In this novel, the flaws in this protagonist were glaringly obvious. She is a PI without the first clue as to how to initiate an investigation. She spends pages declaring that she is the expert and everyone needs to listen to her without actually coming to any conclusions at all, thoroughout the entire course of the novel. The secondary characters were all haphazardly thrown together, and were so inconsistent that I often felt like I was missing a valuable plot point in the apparent sudden onset bipolar disorder that was affecting them all simultaneously. Unfortunately, this was not the case; they were just poorly developed.<br /><br />Thirdly, the dialogue. Dear lord in heaven above, the dialogue. October used the 'I know it's not a plan, but do you have a better idea?' line approximately six times. Conversations skipped between topics with absolutely no direction. Characters were constantly posturing or threatening with no reason or regard for the fact that they were stuck in a building where people were being snuffed out at an alarming rate. <br /><br />Forthly, the plot. I almost can't believe this was published, it was so plodding and poorly developed. It read like a corny horror movie (oh no, something mysterious is happening <i>over there</i>, you must go check it out. Oh no, communication with the outside has been diabled. Oh no, we are dying when we end up alone in this creepy building, but let's none of us stick together. Oh no, there is a pressing and important reason why no one can come to our aid and yet we cannot just leave the dangerous place. Oh no, the killer must be one of us.). They established that it was someone on the inside who was killing the others, but never tried to actually narrow this down. Everyone wandered around by themselves, and other than lecturing them that it was dangerous, Toby (the miracle detective) had no problem with this. (I would honestly shoot anyone I found by themselves. If you are not concerned that you will be murdered, you must be the murderer *pow, pow*). I addition, there is only the sketchiest reason they all stayed in the building where they were being murdered. I mean, if you were worried about April, why didn't everyone but April and Jan leave the building? Ta da! And how was April going to get hurt, anyway? She was a frigging computer program. So much stupid in one book.<br /><br />I couldn't even finish this. I skipped to the last two chapters, verified that I was right about who-dunnit and what the heck was up with Alex/whats-her-face, and read the villain monologue about why this senseless plotline was inflicted on me. Although <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6294549.Rosemary_and_Rue__October_Daye___1_" title="Rosemary and Rue (October Daye, #1) by Seanan McGuire" rel="nofollow noopener">Rosemary and Rue</a> was incredibly slow to start, it at least went somewhere and made sense according to the characters and their rules. This book was a terrible parody of a murder mystery, with cardboard characters, and the repetitive writing of author trying to beat us overhead with the plot points she <i>did</i> come up with, in the hopes that it will distract us from the gaping holes. <br /><br />This book is on my 'incomplete' list because I could not inflict it on myself any longer, and I will not be reading any more of this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17611302723200405570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_416101606" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/416101606" />
    <a title="Heidi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5812324-heidi"><img alt="Heidi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489091071p2/5812324.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/416101606?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi" href="/user/show/5812324-heidi">Heidi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer416101606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7134769418831690123">Friends! I’ve finally done it, I’ve found another Urban Fantasy series I think I’m going to love. There were concerns as I ventured past the world of Ilona Andrews. I tried a couple of new starts, and came away disappointed and worried that all other UF had a lackluster sheen to it. Toby Daye and I got off to an okay start, enough to make me interested in checking out A Local Habitation, and I’m so glad I did. In book two of the October Daye series Seanan McGuire really finds her stride, and I’m</span>
  <span id="freeText7134769418831690123" style="display:none">Friends! I’ve finally done it, I’ve found another Urban Fantasy series I think I’m going to love. There were concerns as I ventured past the world of Ilona Andrews. I tried a couple of new starts, and came away disappointed and worried that all other UF had a lackluster sheen to it. Toby Daye and I got off to an okay start, enough to make me interested in checking out A Local Habitation, and I’m so glad I did. In book two of the October Daye series Seanan McGuire really finds her stride, and I’m happy to say she had me right there with her the whole way through.<br /><br /><i>The hero’s journey has suffered in modern years. Once we could’ve gotten a knight in shining armor riding to the rescue, pennants flying. These days you’re lucky to get a battered changeling and her underage, half-trained assistant, and the princesses are confused technological wizards in the towers of silicon and steel. Standards aren’t what they used to be.</i><br /><br />It’s been six months since the closing pages of Rosemary and Rue. Toby Daye has renewed her P.I. license and is working once again. Of course, her renewed connections with the fae world mean that when her liege calls, she answers, and this time Sylvester’s sending her to the County of Tamed Lightening to check on his niece, Countess January O’Leary. What Toby finds is a strange fea-run tech company where employees have been dropping dead under mysterious circumstances. She has to find the murderer and stop who or what it is from killing off the rest of the company one by one–Toby and her sidekick Quentin included.<br /><br />Not only did Seanan McGuire hit her stride in A Local Habitation, this is also where Toby really finds her voice. She needed to go through the harsh growth process allotted to her in Rosemary and Rue, but here Toby has accepted her place in fae society and gained a few more hard edges to get her by. We finally see her P.I. skills and experience clicking into place, unfortunately for her (though fortunate for our personal entertainment), it’s in a situation where the natural talents she brings to the table as a Daoine Sidhe are useless. We see how Toby’s number one priority is the safety of those around her, and how past failures continue to weigh heavily on her heart. I’ll admit that it was a relief to see Toby put the past behind her in order to deal with the present in A Local Habitation. She’s obviously very aware of her past–what happened with Luna and Raysel, her daughter, Dare–but they don’t drag her down the way they did in the previous installment. I’m sure each of these things will continue to affect who she is as a character in major ways, but I’ll take a character who’s hardened over one who’s a blubbering mess any day. That said, Toby is still very real and affected emotionally–not hardened beyond her humanity, just sharpened beyond the breaking point.<br /><br />The supporting cast in A Local Habitation brings back some of my favorites from Rosemary and Rue and introduces a crew of interesting new species to the table. Quentin, our proper pure blood ward gets an education as Toby’s newly appointed sidekick, and it’s easy to see why she has a soft spot for the kid. There’s more Connor selkie goodness, and even better, more Tybalt. I felt as if we barely saw Tybalt in Rosemary and Rue, but it was enough to give me a strong suspicion that I would love him. Now, there’s no doubt that I do–and a Kate &amp; Curran-esque ‘Here, kitty, kitty’ certainly doesn’t hurt matters either. The wait for them to just make out already is kind of killing me, but I love a good slow burn, and I’m thrilled that Toby’s still more or less oblivious to the fact that she has it bad (I may be projecting my desires on her subconscious a bit here). I also love to see the burgeoning friendship developing between two lonely souls, Toby and the Luidaeg. I’m a sucker for old, wise, and crabby characters, and you can’t get much more of any of these things than you do with the Luidaeg.<br /><br />Plus, there’s the plot of A Local Habitation, which I have to admit with no eloquence whatsoever, is flat out awesome. If I felt as if it was somewhat predictable or reminiscent of one of my favorite episodes of Doctor Who (I’m not going to say which one, but you’re welcome to guess), it didn’t detract at all from my enjoyment. Even if I had a vague idea of what was going on, that didn’t explain all of the intricacies to me, and I loved uncovering them as we went along. For the life of me I don’t know how Toby resists strangling those she’s literally bleeding to help when they seem to hinder her at every turn. But then, I suppose, that’s what a good pissed off Cait Sidhe is for.<br /><br />Finally, can I just say that I am such a fan of Seanan McGuire’s covers? Both October Day and her new InCryptid series get covers that accurately represent the characters therein. Unfortunately, this is less common than you’d think. A Local Habitation‘s cover is, to me, the spitting image of Toby complete with Dare’s knife and Tybalt’s jacket, and damn if it doesn’t look good on her.<br /><br />A Local Habitation is an excellent take off to a promising series. It celebrates a perfect balance between the modern technological world and the ancient world of mythology. Add to that an ideal pace, a dash of biting humor, and plenty of action, and you’ve pretty much assured October Daye a place in my heart.<br /><br />Original review posted at <a href="http://bunburyinthestacks.com/review-2/review-a-local-habitation-by-seanan-mcguire/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bunbury in the Stacks</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7134769418831690123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Ina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13594589-ina"><img alt="Ina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562661735p2/13594589.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1903299371?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ina" href="/user/show/13594589-ina">Ina</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10362757129279418541"><b>
  <u>Re-read: 20/11/2017</u>
</b><br/><b>4 stars</b><br/><br/>Seeing my original review is a little bit funny, because first time I read this series, I enjoyed the first book much more than this one, while now it's the other way around. When I started re-reading this series, I wasn’t sure why I gave it such good rating the first time I read it. Luckily, I’m starting to remember now. Even though there is a plenty of deaths (seriously, a lot of deaths) in this one, it’s still much lighter than the first installment. We get more </span>
  <span id="freeText10362757129279418541" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Re-read: 20/11/2017</u>
</b><br /><b>4 stars</b><br /><br />Seeing my original review is a little bit funny, because first time I read this series, I enjoyed the first book much more than this one, while now it's the other way around. When I started re-reading this series, I wasn’t sure why I gave it such good rating the first time I read it. Luckily, I’m starting to remember now. Even though there is a plenty of deaths (seriously, a lot of deaths) in this one, it’s still much lighter than the first installment. We get more Quentin and a little bit more Tybalt and less Toby getting shot (seriously, besides almost being blown up, she was basically healthy throughout the first two thirds of the book! Nicely done, Tobes!)<br /><br />However, I stand by my statement from the review of the first book. Toby has a terrible taste in men. First there was her mortal husband who got mad at her when they found her after fourteen years (I mean, she was found naked in the park so it obviously looked like kidnapping or something like that and he got MAD because she left them? Not cool), then Devin, Alex (who I am not even going to comment on) and Connor. I’m sorry, but how am I supposed to be rooting for him when the first thing he did when he found out Toby and Quentin were in the accident (and almost died) was getting mad at her for leaving something in the car that blew up? I’m sorry, what? You find out that someone you care about almost exploded in the freakin car and you get mad at them because they didn’t take something from the burning car? Again, not cool.<br /><br />At least there’s Tybalt to balance all of these morons out, because Toby would be doomed otherwise.<br /><br />P.S.: I love how Toby and Luidaeg went from "want to kill you" to "feeding seagulls together". What a nice friendship.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Original review: 5/2/2017</u>
</b><br /><b>3.5 - 4 stars</b><br /><br />Even though I didn't enjoy this installment as much as I enjoyed the first one (mostly because I officially fell in love with Tybalt and there wasn't nearly as much of him as I would have liked), <b>I'm officially hooked!</b><br /><br />I read some reviews and <b>a lot of people complained about plot twists being predictable</b> - obviously, everyone knew who the killer is from the beginning. <b>Well, call me stupid, because I didn't.</b> I had some suspicions, but at various points of the book, I suspected every single character, so I can't say I knew who it was all along. (I mean, I suspected someone and then it turned out it COULDN'T have been them. Even if it could). <br /><br />And the twist with Alex and Terrie didn't seem so predictable to me either. I thought they were <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[some kind of love inducing Fae, but I really didn't know they were the same person. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Once again, feel free to call me fool. <br /><br /><b>And this book contained a lot of things I like in UF:</b><br />- strange pets (hi, Spike!), <br />- great friends (Sylvester, Luna), <br />- intriguing people you are scared of, yet you are strangely attracted to them (Tybalt, Luidaeg),<br />- teenage sidekicks (Quentin),<br />- mysteries I really wanted to find out answers to (Who was the killer? What was the deal with Alex? What was the deal with the freakin cats? What was the secret behind the AHL?)<br />- main female character I actually understand (I know, I know, some of you think that Toby made some stupid choices. Okay. In my opinion, she mostly picked the best out of her bad options)<br /><br /><b>The only thing I still don't like is Toby's love life. I mean, that girl has a terrible taste. Here's to hoping she will jump into Tybalt's arms SOON.</b><br /><br />P.S.: This series has a really high body count. We are only two books into the story and how many people have already died? Ten? Wow. And can Toby do something right? I mean, she keeps letting people down and even though it's not her fault, she still blames herself for it. Give my girl a break!<br /><br />P.S.2: From now on, I'm saying "Oberon's balls" instead of "Damn".<br /><br />P.S.3: How on Earth is Toby still alive? I mean, she almost bled to death like five times already.<br /><br />P.S.4: I can't wait to see what future holds for <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[April <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

    <div class="updateActionLinks">

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7247640-kira?shelf=fae">fae</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7247640-kira?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer250962164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3035953188484258149">2011: 5 stars<br/>2014: 4 stars<br/>2016: 3.5 stars<br/><br/>I can definitely say this is my least favorite book in the series. I get a little more annoyed with it each time I read it. Toby is sent to Fremont to check on Sylvester’s niece since he can’t reach her. When Toby arrives, January claims it's Sylvester who isn’t responding to her calls, so Toby realizes something weird is going on. Then it isn’t long before people start dying. <br/><br/>The characters in Fremont weren’t interesting. Gordon was a bitch. Alex and Ter</span>
  <span id="freeText3035953188484258149" style="display:none">2011: 5 stars<br />2014: 4 stars<br />2016: 3.5 stars<br /><br />I can definitely say this is my least favorite book in the series. I get a little more annoyed with it each time I read it. Toby is sent to Fremont to check on Sylvester’s niece since he can’t reach her. When Toby arrives, January claims it's Sylvester who isn’t responding to her calls, so Toby realizes something weird is going on. Then it isn’t long before people start dying. <br /><br />The characters in Fremont weren’t interesting. Gordon was a bitch. Alex and Terrie were off-putting, and everyone else was unmemorable. They were dropping like flies, and I didn’t care. I didn’t understand their reactions to the murders. No one in Fremont did much of anything to solve the murders or prevent them aside from Toby and Quinton. None of them had any sense of self preservation either. For such smart people they acted like idiots. <br /><br />Toby did some interesting things with magic. It really makes you wonder what else she is capable of. Aside from that I wasn’t too impressed with her. She was extremely bossy. There was a lot of childish bickering among all of the characters. It was boring and repetitive at times. Tybalt stole the show. The scene at the beginning when he assisted drunken Toby home is one of my favorite. The main plot isn’t significant to the overarching storyline, but Toby did learn some things that are important later on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3035953188484258149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3451139124" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3451139124" />
    <a title="Di Maitland" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/112155925-di-maitland"><img alt="Di Maitland" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585661189p2/112155925.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3451139124?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Di Maitland" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Di Maitland" href="/user/show/112155925-di-maitland">Di Maitland</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=non-humans">non-humans</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=titled-characters">titled-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=action-girl">action-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=faeries">faeries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=celtic">celtic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=very-old-characters">very-old-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/112155925-di-maitland?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3451139124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2041529688524291202"><blockquote>
  <i>"I recommend wearing something clingy as that may distract him from whatever he wishes to lecture you about this time. Hopefully it’s your manners. You are truly endearing when you sleep. I attribute this to the exotic nature of seeing you in a state of silence. Tybalt."</i>
</blockquote><br/>I picked this book up when I was looking for an easy listen that wouldn't strain the brain cells. On that, it delivered. Unfortunately, it fell just short of delivering on much else.<br/><br/>When Toby's liege, Sylvester, asks her to c</span>
  <span id="freeText2041529688524291202" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"I recommend wearing something clingy as that may distract him from whatever he wishes to lecture you about this time. Hopefully it’s your manners. You are truly endearing when you sleep. I attribute this to the exotic nature of seeing you in a state of silence. Tybalt."</i>
</blockquote><br />I picked this book up when I was looking for an easy listen that wouldn't strain the brain cells. On that, it delivered. Unfortunately, it fell just short of delivering on much else.<br /><br />When Toby's liege, Sylvester, asks her to check in on his niece, January, after she stops answering his calls, Toby heads for ALH, Jan's software business. With her is Quentin, one of Sylvester's Fae pages, who's looking to broaden his horizons. What they find is a company in disarray but no one willing to admit what's wrong. Together they must win the trust of the employees, discover the problem and find the culprit - all before they end up a victim themselves.<br /><br />Despite her job title of Private Investigator, Toby shows little ability to investigate. If the blood doesn't tell her who did it, and the culprit doesn't speak up, Toby's a little stuck. Worse are her maternalistic tendencies. I usually like a motherly figure in my fiction, but Toby isn't homely; she's not going to make you cookies and tuck you into bed. Instead, she seems to see herself as some sort of hip mentor: down with the kids whilst simultaneously trying to teach those kids essential life skills. I found it grating.<br /><br />Quentin is a stereotypical, well-meaning, over-eager teenage boy, narrated in a high-pitched voice. He was the only other character I really felt I had a hold on. January was too elusive to really get to know, and April, her daughter, too alien - or maybe psychotic is a better word for her. (Have you noticed all the names-that-are-months yet? There's a May in the next book, too.) Alex fell short of charming and hit sleazy, and Gordon seemed to be stuck on her angry setting. The rest of them, sad to say, mostly blended into one for me.<br /><br />Connor and Tybalt make an appearance - thank goodness or the book might have been demoted to 2.5*s. I'm still gutted that Connor's taken and Toby's too morally upstanding to do much anyway. Tybalt's a solid stand-in but needs to soften a little and try for something that isn't snarky.<br /><br />I didn't dislike the book. The world building was wonderful and I find all of the different strains of Fae fascinating. I just felt like it fell short of where it could have been, and it could have been great.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2041529688524291202" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ff5Bk5v/9Myt+B9PCtnZMK9YAHmjlRqOK7RdiJrmyukp1V4Fua3yr96cnYFDZO1kxlqTzWbFlV5C8799903Y6A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('p+4wOSfqAsp1B4pCmM3mSRruwIYOHnQKKFTtDvnx4O3zxS+vBbgEqQZjCIzRcNIdc+xTMstO+9pBEw/7lFry7A==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer10152769218006081431">Hi! I'm Seanan McGuire, author of the Toby Daye series (<i>Rosemary and Rue</i>, <i>A Local Habitation</i>, <i>An Artificial Night</i>, <i>Late Eclipses</i>), as well as a lot of other things. I'm also Mira Grant (<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.miragrant.com'>www.miragrant.com</a>), author of <i>Feed</i> and <i>Deadline</i>.<br/><br/>Born and raised in Northern California, I fear weather and am remarkably laid-back about rattlesnakes. I watch too many horror movies, read too many comic books, and </span>
  <span id="freeText10152769218006081431" style="display:none">Hi! I'm Seanan McGuire, author of the Toby Daye series (<i>Rosemary and Rue</i>, <i>A Local Habitation</i>, <i>An Artificial Night</i>, <i>Late Eclipses</i>), as well as a lot of other things. I'm also Mira Grant (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.miragrant.com">www.miragrant.com</a>), author of <i>Feed</i> and <i>Deadline</i>.<br /><br />Born and raised in Northern California, I fear weather and am remarkably laid-back about rattlesnakes. I watch too many horror movies, read too many comic books, and share my house with two monsters in feline form, Lilly and Alice (Siamese and Maine Coon).<br /><br />I <i>do not</i> check this inbox. Please don't send me messages through Goodreads; they won't be answered. I don't want to have to delete this account. :(</span>
